RATING: 8
The Good: Production quality is top-of-the-line. The minis, cards, map tiles, and dice are all excellent quality. The rules are simple, but the game is not without its intricacies.  The base game includes a lengthy campaign, as well as the option of skirmish play. The main characters, while created for the game, "feel" like Star Wars characters, at least as far as they're fleshed out (which isn't much). The game is strategic and fun, although I prefer All VS The Game to 1 VS All games.

The Bad: Fantasy Flight includes main characters in token form only, forcing you to buy the separate figure/card packs to flesh out the game. The gameplay can be incredibly repetitive, too, but that is tied to the type of game that it is. Scenarios offer different objectives, but they do not change gameplay much.

RATING: 7
I was super pumped to get this game on release, but I never got a group together. I even felt like I wasted cash on a Broken Token insert and multiple expansions. The best I could do was to play it in an simple version with my son.

I even printed up the custom solo variant by RedJak, but never felt the compulsion to try it.

But now the game hits my table thanks to the Legends of the Alliance app! I was looking for a campaign mode for Mansions of Madness 2E, and luckily this delivers what I was looking for without needing more purchases (I havenât played Descent).

The game is very much a tactical strategy game (akin to XCOM the video game), with very mild RPG elements. It feels good, especially with the constant drip of new items and abilities to power up the heroes. Because the game emphasizes combat, you will see each Imperial model in your collection repeatedly, which makes things a little bland. Map setup can be cumbersome with its plethora of small and odd shaped pieces. But the game is fun, and I am greatful for FFG to invigorate new life into the product basically for free.

RATING: 4
Too much of a war-game to be a good RPG, too much luck to be a good board-game, too constricted to be a good war-game.  
I must admit that, given the hype, I was expecting the same 'wow' moment I got from playing X-Wing the first time. Sadly IA is nowhere near the same league. Or even the same galaxy. 
Loooong mission set up times, more snoozing between player turns, and a game system that is almost solely based on lucky dice rolls. To be fair X-Wing is dice driven as well, but X-Wing doesn't take 2 hours+ per mission...
The worst part of the game however are the 'pop-up' baddies that totally destroy any game immersion. In our third game we had 3 storm troopers, a crewed E-Web blaster AND an AT-ST walker just appear in our area. "Where the heck did they come from?" We asked the GM. After considering for a minute: "Erm, they were hiding behind a locker?"

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
I really want to like this game.  I like the theme and I like the idea that doing missions have effects on later missions, but everything just feels so horribly balanced in the Empire's favor that it's not fun.

It's crazy because this is a game where we, the rebel players, have to go up against a larger group of ever-spawning enemies.  You'd think that because of the overwhelming numbers we'd have in general stats than those enemies but you'd be wrong.  We may have anywhere from 2-3 more HP than the enemies, but our attacks are much weaker.  In a single turn, the Empire player can almost take down a player where we get happy when we do 2 damage.

But that's when we even hit the player because we also have worse defenses.  Where we either have a single white (bad) or black (good) defense die, the Empire player almost always seems to have black dice, multiple dice, and/or things that buffs their defense.  As a Force Adept it literally feels like I'm running up to a probe droid and waving a wet noodle in its face.  Even the wookiee isn't doing much better.  Most of our damage comes from unblockable things like cleave and blast, but unfortunately that's an insignificant amount of damage.

That said, when we do manage to damage an enemy, the infinitely spawning probe droids just heal whatever is hurt.  When we aren't doing damage, the probe droids proceed to murder us.  In the off chance we get close to killing a probe droid, it just explodes on us and another spawns.

Fighting in that game is just hopeless for the rebel players.  We tried the first few missions killing enemies and we were just getting our butts handed to us.  So this most recent mission we tried running since fighting was pretty inefective.  That mostly worked, until half way through the mission a weakened slow person needed to be escorted through a gauntlet of enemies we left behind.

See, these missions are puzzles that you have zero way of knowing the right answer.  If you fight, you die.  If you ignore enemies, they catch up and murder you or eventually kill your goal.

Nothing just feels right in this game because it feels so unbalanced.  The Empire player gets to constantly respawn, they have gadgets like cloaking that gives them more dice, jet packs that let them ignore terrain, and all sorts of bonuses that help them out.  THe rebel players get some powers and equipment, but at a much slower pace so we're constantly outclassed.

I like a difficult game, but this game just isn't fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The light side:
Surprisingly great game even if I wasn't a star wars fanboy. Bought it for the theme and minis. Also wanted to try painting and as I missed out on Descent a redo in SW universe seemed like a good time to try it out. Turns out the game itself is also very good. So far only played skirmish but there is a real tactical fight there, not only a dicefest. Excited on seeing how good the game continues to be after the expansions.

The dark-side:
Initial feeling with the expansions is that they are an outright moneygrab by FFG. This is the only negative thing about the game. Comparing the base-game versus the equally expensive full first wave of expansions I have to say the current FFG mini-expansion model feels like a complete rip-off. One can only draw one conclusion, FFG are the EA of boardgames. It should not be legal that they hook me with the base game providing 100% fun, then charge me the same for mini-expansions that only provide 20% more content. And even worse is the model that they withhold content from the base-game and split it up into mini-expansions, I'm looking at the missions and command cards especially. In the long run FFGs actions will bring about their own demise, if karma exists... which I doubt.
Why can't FFG do the honorable thing and simply release big and small-box expansions with a fair price instead of this business model based on leeching "whales".

Rating changed to 10 after campaign play has proven itself. The game has a good desperate atmosphere and my fears of the campaign being a dud were unfounded. The twists and turns have really challenged us and the character development has clear progression from peashooter to ultimate killing machines. Still hating the business model but I have gotten decent value on my investment.

Rating changed to 9.5 after a few more campaign missions. For us 2/4 side missions have been an absolute pain to play and are based on the sole mechanic of deatmatch... this does not work in IA. I hope we just happened to pick the only two side missions that absolutely suck. Story missions have so far not let us down.

Rating dropped to 8 after finishing the base game campaign. The campaign was so imbalanced it was mostly a lesson in futility for the rebels after the half-way point of the campaign. At that point there was really no reason to play, we had practically lost before even starting. Imperial powerups had made the ordinary cannon fodder stormtroopers have boosted health and more firepower than a hero. A single activation by the imperial player always resulted in a wounded hero if they got in range of a healthy hero. Rating for campaign: 6. I know this campaign might be balanced in some gamegroups but I also know that in those groups they chose the stupid one to play the imperial side. Only reason this stays above an 8 is that the skirmish still works and the campaign wasn't all bad at the beginning before powerups and unachievable objectives destroyed it. But I expected more/at least some balance when paying premium price. None of us, imperial player included could think of any other way for the rebels to win than by epic dicethrowing. We tried playing smart, only killed those we had to to prevent getting wounded. We tried playing hard, killing everyone. We tried running through. The outcome was always the same, imperial victory by a large margin. Also the scripted events are mostly just plain stupid! How are the rebel heroes supposed to know that this time you shouldn't advance the mission and that you should position yourself in a certain way or be doomed to fail.

My only concern about the game is that after playing it once or twice then some of the missions won't be so exciting (because all the hidden information will be known), but the good thing here is that many missions aren't played in a single play through so there is a degree of inherent longevity there, and also I am sure FFG will release quite a few expansions to keep things fresh (which, personally, I enjoy expanding my games).  And finally, the saving point here is that after playing 10 or so missions then odds are you may remember some vague things about the first few missions, but probably won't remember (as rebels) exactly where the Imperial reinforcement points were, or exactly what happened when the door opened.

As always with FFG, the components are of the highest quality. They have really spoiled my buddies and I there, everything else we play we seem to find lacking.

RATING: 10
I love this game. Particularly skirmish mode. The set up time is the clunkiest part, especially for new skirmish players since there are so many options but it's a great collection of flavor in the characters (especially the mercenaries) which corresponds to cool actions they can do. There is a decent amount of luck to the game when it comes to rolling dice but the strategy really comes in to setting up your troops and embracing character abilities. Also there's tremendous replay value. I would play this any time I get the chance.

Update 6/2016: I increased it to 10. Every time I play a skirmish I love it more because of its intricacies and want to play it more. Yes I love Star Wars in general but that's not all that's at work. It's the fact that every game is a tense game where there isn't a clear leader for a few rounds. Several times I've had a commanding lead for points and board placement only to lose it in the end or vice versa. Part of that is dice rolls, part of that is that most skirmish maps have at least 2 distinct things going on such as multiple ways to score extra points or damaging effects caused by things separate from the main objective. You can half ass go after both locations and possibly get mowed over if your opponent goes all in on 1 of the 2 or you sent a scout 1 way to do something to lure 1 or 2 of their people away, or blah blah blah. It's fun.

Then the Star Wars flavor on top of that makes it even more fun. Just because I can quasi relate to the characters having seen the movies, shows, read books, etc countless times. So despite 1 character maybe not being the easiest to do well with, I want to make them work so I keep trying new variations to a build to make them more effective. 

Anyways, I could go on forever. Solid 10.0 in my book. Best game in my collection. 

Update 5/2017: About 1/3 of the way through my first campaign (Return to Hoth) as the Imperial Player and it's still really fun. But as the Imperial that has 30+ skirmish plays, it's important to not go for the throat and play at your absolute best otherwise you will crush morale so much nobody will want to play after back to back to back losses. They're good losers when they lose but it feels hopeless after a while. So play nice if they're new!

RATING: 7
[i]Preliminary mid-campaign rating from an unexperienced Rebel player perspective:[/i]

I'm a born eurogamer so these kind of games aren't really for me. That said, I still think that Imperial Assault is really cool. I love the theme and the overall flow of the gameplay. I wish the campaign was more immersive though, every mission feels like a separate bit, there's no continuous narrative. 

The only major downside I've encountered so far is the fact that the campaign missions are rather unballanced - one side often has a distinct advantage over the other and this can be pretty frustrating, especially if you come from a eurogaming background (but maybe the missions are supposed to be unballanced and they were intentionally designed as such).

I only know a small portion of the game - I've yet to play as an "overlord" and I've never tried the skirmish mode so far. Once I get the hold of every aspect of the game the rating might go up (and it probably will). All in all, if you like Star Wars universe and enjoy ameritrash style of gaming then Imperial Assault is a must-have.

RATING: 7.5
If you know me, you know that I love Star Wars (the original trilogy, anyway). I grew up with it. I made friends through it. In a very roundabout sort of way, I met my wife because of it. And as long as I've loved Star Wars, I've loved Star Wars games. Particularly, the Star Wars RPG.

So, when I finally got a chance to pick up this game, I was fairly impressed. The theme is well-represented, the components are great and the game play is action-packed. Playing it feels like a Star Wars adventure.

So, what is it that holds this game back a bit for me? The answer is a little complicated but it boils down to a few basic complaints. The core system can get a little cluttered at times, which can slow down the action. With so many abilities, symbols and conditional rules, it can feel a little too big for its britches once in a while. Also, the delicate balance of the Imperial player's game can be awkward. I rather suspect that once the co-op app is released for this game, some of these issues will be addressed and the game could stand to climb quite a bit higher for me.

As it is, even with a few warts, it's still a great game with lots of appeal.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
This game is a bit of a hard one to rate for me.  Star Wars was such an integral part of my childhood, it is impossible to objectively review this game as just a game, but I will try.

There are two main modes of play, campaign and skirmish.  Campaign mode in my experience has been hit or miss depending on the mission.  On some levels, the rebels are vastly out matched and will have a difficult time winning.  On other levels, it is less of a challenge.  The rebel players have to play a lot of the levels perfectly to have a shot at winning and hope that imperial player makes a mistake they can take advantage of or lucky rolling.  This changes from mission to mission based on the number of rebel players.  With 3 rebel heros, one gets an extra activation per round.  This makes some tasks much more manageable.  Especially when they have to rush to interact with certain things.  With 4 heros, these maps are more challenging.  Overall it is both fun and frustrating to play through.  Unlike other games that have a dungeon master who's job it is to make the game challenging, interesting, but winnable (with some potentially difficult decisions), this game pits one imperial player against all other players.  If the map favors the imperial player, and the imperial player doesn't show mercy or pull the punches a bit, it can be a painful experience for the rebel players.  As the imperial player you have to sometimes act more like a DM than an actual player.  It's a bit hard while the rebels constantly mow through your troopers and other figures like they were paper dolls to create a situation that is winnable for the rebels when it is in your favor.  It just feels good to be about finally give them a good beating.  The imperial player also has pre-knowledge of certain locations on the map that will be important allowing them to huddle troops there or do other things that make the missions really hard for rebels but are thematically wonky.  I once had a Nexu that could have attacked a player, like a Nexu probably would with disregard for anything else.  Instead, I used it to block a walkway creating a separation between the two groups of the rebel team causing them to have to defeat the Nexu before regrouping, wasting a round taking care of that instead of completing the mission objectives.  As a result, they failed by a few activations.  Strategically the move was the best for my "team".  It wasn't very thematic and ruined the feel of the whole match.  Campaign mode is rife with these types of issues where the imperial player often has to play in the spirit of the characters and map rather than play to win, otherwise it can ruin the game for everyone.

Skirmish mode is a completely different mode of playing this game, and one that I really enjoy.  You "deck-build" your team of figures and your command cards to create your squad.  Only then do you find out what mission you will play.  So you might form a heavy hitting, small quantity, and slow moving team only to find out that the mission requires a bit more mobility, or via versa.  You have to figure out how to adapt your team to best meet the goals and defeat the other team.  There is ton of potential to customize your group and find all kinds of interesting groups to bring down.  This currently only plays 2 people, though I hear the next full expansion coming out will open skirmish mode to 4 player matches.  Skirmish mode ends up being a lot more tactical.  You adjust to what your player is doing.  Campaign mode is a bit more strategic.  You have mission objectives and while you might have to handle things that come up that the imperial player does, often you have to ignore them and just grind towards the goal regardless.  It is that tactical feel of skirmish that I like.  You can't just follow a plan coming into a match.  You have to carefully decide which figures to use in which order to maximize your damage potential, minimize the damage you could take, or limit the options or your opponent.  Each move matters and is important.  Where as in campaign mode "move towards the objective" is often one, if not both, of the actions on nearly half of the turns.

With all that said, it is a solid game where a couple of mistakes can be the difference between winning a match and losing a match.  It is great to see the power shifting slightly back and forth and you see people make slight mistakes and see how finely balanced the game is (at least in skirmish mode).  

I would probably give this game an 8 or so if it was themed differently.  But with a star wars theme, I just can't help but want to play it, even if the matches are sometimes frustrating.  It still is very enjoyable to be in the Star Wars world controlling the characters.  And for me, that just puts it over the top.

RATING: 6.5
Unsurprisingly, skirmish mode doesn't appeal to me at all.  Lighthearted killing belongs in multiplayer bash-a-thons such as King of Tokyo, Star Wars Epic Duels, Nexus Ops, and Bucket King - not in two-player space operas with overly earnest flavor text.

The campaign mode is a shiny iteration of the Descent/Doom system, though not quite good enough to own.  If my kids were younger and had insatiable Star Wars appetites, this would be a sure-fire purchase.  Nowadays Descent 2nd edition delivers the goods for my high-humor adult and family gaming groups, though strictly as light filler.

Imperial Assault's biggest drawback is that the scenarios aren't nearly as interesting as those in Descent.  The Descent designers gave themselves permission to be inventive and nuts, whereas in IA they limited themselves to dry, run-of-the-mill Star Wars serials.  That was not the best choice, as humor and imagination have long been a hallmark of the franchise.

I also hate the expansion model for this one.  I can play [u]with[/u] Han and Chewbacca as allies, but I can't play [u]as[/u] Han and Chewbacca? And I have to pay separately for them?  Bleah.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
First impression isn't what I expected.
Beautiful, inspiring artwork, miniatures and cards. Simple to learn, great campaign system in theory. (Have not played a full campaign, so cannot say)
Limited number of turns are a big turn off. They encourage a single style of play: "run for the objectives, ignore all else". The "DM" has multiple ways of winning and knows the conditions and upcoming surprises while the players do not. 
There's great potential for fun, but my first impression was one of frustration. Limited options, a single way of winning while the DM has two to three (time limit, wounding the heroes, blocking the objectives) and the statistical probability of victory seems highly stacked against the heroes.
I know for a fact that this game is fun and I want it to be, but I may look at alternative ways of playing or house rules.
